  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_36c12842-d779-4192-bd84-018546a1f963'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer14671428775861781108">When Adriana, a brilliant young archaeologist, accepts a position at the Museum of Archaeology in her hometown of Santander, Spain, she never imagines that her new boss has lived through the history she can only study.<br/><br/>Iago, the charismatic technical director of the museum, is more than ten thousand years old but appears to be only thirty-five. Iago and his family are longe</span>
  <span id="freeText14671428775861781108" style="display:none">When Adriana, a brilliant young archaeologist, accepts a position at the Museum of Archaeology in her hometown of Santander, Spain, she never imagines that her new boss has lived through the history she can only study.<br /><br />Iago, the charismatic technical director of the museum, is more than ten thousand years old but appears to be only thirty-five. Iago and his family are longevos—people who never seem to age after reaching adulthood. The ancient family is divided: Iago’s brother and sister seek the source of their longevity in hopes of creating more like themselves, while Iago and his father fear the repercussions of the true Fountain of Youth.<br /><br />A dangerous game of power and knowledge that has played out over eons becomes even more complicated when Adriana attracts both brothers’ attention—and learns their secret.<br /><br />Filled with science, history, and passion, The Immortal Collection transports the reader through time and space, from the days of cavemen, through the Roaring Twenties, to the charming plazas of contemporary Spain. Ancient history meets cutting-edge research in this modern love story and sweeping historical saga.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14671428775861781108" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_910154652" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/910154652" />
    <a title="KB Wayne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6001750-kb-wayne"><img alt="KB Wayne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370189321p2/6001750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/910154652?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="KB Wayne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="KB Wayne" href="/user/show/6001750-kb-wayne">KB Wayne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/21521748-the-immortal-collection">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer910154652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4124021013900908545">Closer to 3.5 stars.<br/><br/>A few years ago I fell in love with Deborah Harkness' <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11559200.Shadow_of_Night__All_Souls_Trilogy___2_' title='Shadow of Night (All Souls Trilogy, #2) by Deborah Harkness' rel='nofollow noopener'>All Souls Trilogy</a>, the third of which is expected to be released this summer. I'd never ever been a paranormal reader but something about that story just enchanted me -- probably the whimsy combined with the romance (I am a romance reader!).<br/><br/>Reading the description of The Immortal Collection I thought "you bet, I'll try it." And I'm glad I did. It is quite long, the romance quite mild, but the descriptions and the depth of </span>
  <span id="freeText4124021013900908545" style="display:none">Closer to 3.5 stars.<br /><br />A few years ago I fell in love with Deborah Harkness' <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11559200.Shadow_of_Night__All_Souls_Trilogy___2_" title="Shadow of Night (All Souls Trilogy, #2) by Deborah Harkness" rel="nofollow noopener">All Souls Trilogy</a>, the third of which is expected to be released this summer. I'd never ever been a paranormal reader but something about that story just enchanted me -- probably the whimsy combined with the romance (I am a romance reader!).<br /><br />Reading the description of The Immortal Collection I thought "you bet, I'll try it." And I'm glad I did. It is quite long, the romance quite mild, but the descriptions and the depth of story / character were terrific and thorough.<br /><br />Iago is a 10,000+ year-old man in a thirty-odd year-old body; he and his family call themselves <i>longevos</i>. Together they are currently running a pre-history museum in Spain. Adriana is an archaeologist / pre-history specialist in her early-thirties who goes to work at the museum. The Immortal Collection is their story.<br /><br />There are many, many holes in this story -- one which is present in my head right now is the absolute disbelief that in his 10,000+ years Iago had never ever told any of his other paramours / children his story, that in all those relationships he'd never felt the profound connection he did with Adriana. Really? In 10,000+ years? Not once? While my children think I'm as old as the dinosaurs (I'm not), I've been fortunate to experience deep, soul-moving love more than once. I get that that angle juices up the story -- finally!, after 10,000+ years, Iago finds his True Mate. But come on.<br /><br />The epilogue left me disappointed, both in its content and that it was even included -- it signaled a huge cliffhanger but it's my understanding this is a standalone, so ...?<br /><br />However, the author's intricate, detailed writing and descriptions were fantastic, although at times I felt the translation may have been a bit rough. Unfortunately, my Spanish is nowhere near strong enough to have read this in the source language, so I cannot say for certain. Suffice to say I was impressed with the level of detail we were shown, not told, but shown.<br /><br />I think these characters, Iago and Adriana, will stay with me for a while. Who doesn't want to believe in that power of love, of connection, and of finally finding respite?</span>
  <a data-text-id="4124021013900908545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_916621139" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/916621139" />
    <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7906042-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535225568p2/7906042.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/916621139?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/7906042-karen">Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer916621139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7500230001425894683">I enjoyed this, the 1st book of the Collection. <br/><br/>It's well researched & has an interesting setting, which shows that the 3 years it took to write was well spent. Set in Spain in 2012 with chapters being written from the point of view of 2 of the main characters, it's pacy and strongly written.<br/><br/>It was recommended to me by Amazon and at first I felt the book was an American 'sexed up' version of a Mary Stewart novel, her stock novel with a plucky young woman slightly out of her depth with a strong s</span>
  <span id="freeText7500230001425894683" style="display:none">I enjoyed this, the 1st book of the Collection. <br /><br />It's well researched &amp; has an interesting setting, which shows that the 3 years it took to write was well spent. Set in Spain in 2012 with chapters being written from the point of view of 2 of the main characters, it's pacy and strongly written.<br /><br />It was recommended to me by Amazon and at first I felt the book was an American 'sexed up' version of a Mary Stewart novel, her stock novel with a plucky young woman slightly out of her depth with a strong silent male who isn't all he seems. But then as I read on, I realised that threaded through the story was the Twilight theme. Luckily the book has enough original features to save it from being just another Fan Fiction. But it's a little disconcerting wondering when the next Twilight part will emerge. <br /><br />On finishing the book I read the bio at the back of my Kindle and saw that the writer is actually Spanish, which explains the competent background and that the American flavour must actually come from the translator. Ms Saenz's research on ancient history is extensive and comes across well throughout the book.<br /><br />I like the book enough that I am interested to know what will happen in the 2nd book, but I really do hope that the Twilight Fan Fiction part is left out so it leaves what could be an excellent story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7500230001425894683" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_940593823" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/940593823" />
    <a title="Tamzin Dunn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28009847-tamzin-dunn"><img alt="Tamzin Dunn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420804951p2/28009847.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tamzin Dunn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tamzin Dunn" href="/user/show/28009847-tamzin-dunn">Tamzin Dunn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer940593823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6267187358125614157">Very interesting and engrossing book. An immortal story with no vampires what a delightful change. The beginning is wonderful and a neat way to start the book as it catches your interest straight away. The immortals are just normal people don't appear to age after about 30 years and have lived for a ridiculously long time, we are talking thousands of years. They don't know why and are trying to find out now that science has reach a stage they can investigate. The research going into this book is</span>
  <span id="freeText6267187358125614157" style="display:none">Very interesting and engrossing book. An immortal story with no vampires what a delightful change. The beginning is wonderful and a neat way to start the book as it catches your interest straight away. The immortals are just normal people don't appear to age after about 30 years and have lived for a ridiculously long time, we are talking thousands of years. They don't know why and are trying to find out now that science has reach a stage they can investigate. The research going into this book is amazing both the medical and historical which was very detailed going back to the stone age, completely fascinating. <br />I found the one down side for me was the romance between Adriana (in her 30s) and Iago (over 10,000 years old). In a word it was boring, I liked both characters but together there was no spark. That said I would be happy to read the next book as there are a few questions remaining unanswered and I care enough to find out what happens next.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1085280024" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1085280024" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2988548-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405106952p2/2988548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1085280024?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/2988548-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2988548-rebecca?shelf=thought-provoking">thought-provoking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2988548-rebecca?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1085280024" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5068628033102335438">I got halfway through this and had to give it up. The story wasn't interesting enough to justify wading through another 350 pages.<br/><br/>"The Immortal Collection" is an extremely long book with an interesting premise--a family of long lived humans who've been around for 10,000 years are looking for the secret to their good health. They have to pick up and move every few decades so people don't notice them not aging. As the story opens, the family runs a museum and does genetic research, seeking the ans</span>
  <span id="freeText5068628033102335438" style="display:none">I got halfway through this and had to give it up. The story wasn't interesting enough to justify wading through another 350 pages.<br /><br />"The Immortal Collection" is an extremely long book with an interesting premise--a family of long lived humans who've been around for 10,000 years are looking for the secret to their good health. They have to pick up and move every few decades so people don't notice them not aging. As the story opens, the family runs a museum and does genetic research, seeking the answer to their immortality in their cells. Adriana, a hot, 30 something historian gets brought into the museum to sell off its collection. Adriana has "ISSUES" from her mother's suicide and estrangement from her father, but I found myself not caring because she isn't that likable. Two of the immortal brothers have the hots for her, but I didn't care about that either. There was a somewhat interesting debate about telomere shortening causing cell aging, but I can pick that up faster from a textbook. <br /><br />This novel was well-written but dull. It's possible that the passion and purpose of the story got lost in the translation from the original Spanish.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5068628033102335438" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer959877416" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer155562940050441360">Don't start this book unless you have a day to kill. I found myself going back to it more and more, for longer periods and I stayed up all night to finish it. <br/>This is about a small family of long-living people and how they live their lives with glimpses back to their lives in the sometimes very distant past. It's not a perfect book but the characters are interesting enough, just don't expect a lot of subtleties.<br/>The real attraction of this book for me was the history and archaeology. A question r</span>
  <span id="freeText155562940050441360" style="display:none">Don't start this book unless you have a day to kill. I found myself going back to it more and more, for longer periods and I stayed up all night to finish it. <br />This is about a small family of long-living people and how they live their lives with glimpses back to their lives in the sometimes very distant past. It's not a perfect book but the characters are interesting enough, just don't expect a lot of subtleties.<br />The real attraction of this book for me was the history and archaeology. A question running throughout the book is who has the rights over discovered relics? The people whose ancestors created the objects or museums who spread knowledge by displaying relics to the public? I want both sides to have their way, it's not always a clear cut issue.<br />I found this book to be an interesting blend of fast-paced fun and thought-provoking history.</span>
  <a data-text-id="155562940050441360" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13441515039676273931">I decided to read the book in English, instead of the Spanish version since English has been my primary language for the last 26-years. I don't now if there are others like me that have to make a decision of what language they should read a book.   <span id="freeText13441515039676273931" style="display:none">I decided to read the book in English, instead of the Spanish version since English has been my primary language for the last 26-years. I don't now if there are others like me that have to make a decision of what language they should read a book. My Spanish is from Puert Rico, and although I have no problems with the language, I felt that I could benefit more from the English version. The book was well written and documented. It kept my attention to the point that I could not put the book down. I've been in Madrid and Santander and It felt so good to read about those 2 beautiful places. The is no cliffhanger at the end, but I am hoping there is going to be a second book, since there is plenty for a second book.</span>

    <a title="Christina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11756085-christina"><img alt="Christina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1344666773p2/11756085.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/908009606?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina" href="/user/show/11756085-christina">Christina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11756085-christina?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer908009606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11543711122345794168">I could not put this book down and spent a few too many nights staying up way too late. It was refreshing to read a book about immortals who weren't vampires, werewolves, mermaids, etc., but who were normal people who happened to live through several millennia. I especially liked that you could see how contemporary events were affected by family members' actions thousands of years ago, hundreds of years ago, or even tens of years ago.<br/><br/>I can't wait for the second book; that cliffhanger was crazy!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_912453490" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/912453490" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11314093-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418275352p2/11314093.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/11314093-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer912453490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10620742314381568724">If you have a basic understanding of genetics. If you believe in Darwinism. If you think all the drama that surrounds family dynamics is interesting......you might like this book. I found it fascinating. A man who is 30,000 years old, and his children. They have a genetic abnormality that allows them to live that long. One of the "ancient family" meets an anthropologist, they fall in love, and this is their story. I look forward to any sequels to this entertaining and original book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Rosemary Dreyer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25514940-rosemary-dreyer"><img alt="Rosemary Dreyer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384319942p2/25514940.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/906120992?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rosemary Dreyer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rosemary Dreyer" href="/user/show/25514940-rosemary-dreyer">Rosemary Dreyer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer906120992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14641176920004966811">Fascinating:<br/>A supernatural novel that spans numerous millennium, The Immortal Collection is a captivating story that involves murder, mystery and a museum. I can't give away any of the plot but encourage you to read this book. While the translation is mostly smooth, there are times when I wished I could read the original Spanish version. Definitely an author to watch for her next novel.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/21521748-the-immortal-collection">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer992829638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9538820483932651763"><strong>Longevos</strong><br/><br/>I was mesmerized by this book. I found the history and science of this book fascinating. I felt the struggle in their complicated family issues. I genuinely hope there is a sequel. I'd recommend this book to all my friends. Thank you so much.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Bwbl6BUIfKX3Qjn0rXsSnq1hGCf2se4a4Hl/FzxDOIEhwDCJadpTx94wYY4xfFj5XxDJA536xB3t2ttjPdBieA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Son idénticas a los asesinatos descritos en la novela Los señores del tiempo: un envenenamiento con la «mosca española» ―la Viagra medieval―, unas víctimas emparedadas como se hacía antaño en el «voto de tinieblas» y un «encubamiento», que consistía en lanzar al río a un preso encerrado en un tonel junto con un gallo, un perro, un gato y una víbora.\n\nLas investigaciones llevarán a Kraken hasta el señor de la torre de Nograro, una casa-torre fortificada habitada ininterrumpidamente desde hace mil años por el primogénito varón. Pero el reverso de tanta nobleza es la tendencia de los señores de la torre a padecer el trastorno de identidad múltiple, un detalle que arrastrará a Estíbaliz a vivir una arriesgada historia de amor. \n\nUnai López de Ayala acabará descubriendo que Los señores del tiempo tiene mucho que ver con su propio pasado. Augusto Ledesma elige el que fuera hogar de James Joyce como primer escenario para continuar su siniestra obra, que alimenta del aliento de sus víctimas y de la humillación de sus perseguidores. Hasta allí se trasladará el inspector Ramiro Sancho en su frenética y obsesiva persecución de un asesino en serie que parece haber acentuado su voracidad.\n\nEntretanto, al otro lado de la frontera, el psicólogo criminalista y exagente del KGB Armando Lopategui, «Carapocha», recorrerá las calles de Belgrado junto a su hija y ahora discípula con el propósito de zanjar cuentas con un pasado despiadado del que no logra despojarse. En otra vuelta de tuerca, a través de fugaces viajes en el tiempo, descubriremos cómo se fraguó la relación entre Pílades y Orestes y asistiremos a su sorprendente desenlace.\n\nTras el rotundo éxito de Memento mori, primera parte de la trilogía Versos, canciones y trocitos de carne, César Pérez Gellida nos conduce de nuevo por los complejos laberintos que conforman la mente criminal desde los ojos de sus protagonistas, ya sean víctimas, asesinos en serie, genocidas o quienes les persiguen. El inesperado desarrollo de los acontecimientos obligará al lector a pasar páginas en una ineludible búsqueda de respuestas.\n\nHaciendo gala de un particular estilo cinematográfico aclamado por la <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer828178185075249586">Eva García Sáenz was born in Vitoria, Spain, in 1972 and she lives in Alicante in Spain's Costa Blanca since she was fifteen.<br/><br/>She is a licensed optometrist and she held various positions in optometry for ten years. Then she worked at the University of Alicante for another eleven years. For three years, she wrote in the evenings to complete "The Immortal Collection," her first novel.<br/><br/>She originally s</span>
  <span id="freeText828178185075249586" style="display:none">Eva García Sáenz was born in Vitoria, Spain, in 1972 and she lives in Alicante in Spain's Costa Blanca since she was fifteen.<br /><br />She is a licensed optometrist and she held various positions in optometry for ten years. Then she worked at the University of Alicante for another eleven years. For three years, she wrote in the evenings to complete "The Immortal Collection," her first novel.<br /><br />She originally self-published on Amazon's Spanish website. Thanks to the enthusiastic reader's reviews, the novel became a bestseller and a literary phenomenon in the social media world. After the book was published traditionally, it hit the print bestseller list as well. The author is currently working on her next book.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="828178185075249586" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
